*Dragon's Maze's* Impact on *Return to Ravnica* Limited
* *by Event Coverage Staff*
[Info](http://archive.wizards.com/Magic/TCG/Events.aspx?x=mtg/event/grandprix/Bangkok13): Fact Sheet





Saturday, 9.00 a.m. - Impact on Limited
---------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

 

Both *Return to Ravnica* and *Gatecrash* have been very enjoyable to draft thus far and there are a plethora of strategies across multiple colors that have been proven to work. Such an interesting block is not without conundrums, especially with the introduction of *Dragon's Maze*.


Previously, players were nudged in the direction of drafting two color decks during the times of triple *Return to Ravnica* as well as triple Gatecrash. Speed, tempo, focus and synergy were not to be neglected, and players who stumbled early often found the game ending faster than they could shout "Ouch!".


Draft decks were much more focused, and the format seemed much faster. Smaller creatures were prized highly and there was often a need for speed, since missing your two or three drop potentially spelt doom.



![Hellhole Flailer++Sluiceway Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Hellhole%20Flailer&options=)
![Hellhole Flailer++Sluiceway Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Sluiceway%20Scorpion&options=)

The Cult of Rakdos steamrolled past their opponents by unleashing oversized threats with no intent to block, coupled with an assortment of efficient removal spells to clear the path. The Golgari Swarm didn't try to compete with speed, but instead tried to stay alive long enough to win the attrition war by generating value out of their slow but powerful scavenge creatures.



![Lyev Skyknight++Call of the Conclave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Lyev%20Skyknight&options=)
![Lyev Skyknight++Call of the Conclave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Call%20of%20the%20Conclave&options=)

The Azorius Senate and Izzet League would not allow that to happen. They took to the air while detaining and removing troublesome blockers like [Trestle Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trestle+Troll)s and [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik)s. The Selesnya Conclave had a different idea on how to amass an army, and aimed to overwhelm by populating additional threats by and backing them up with powerful tricks like [Rootborn Defenses](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rootborn+Defenses).



![Skyknight Legionnaire++Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Skyknight%20Legionnaire&options=)
![Skyknight Legionnaire++Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Cloudfin%20Raptor&options=)

Fast forward three months into *Gatecrash*, players were trying to survive the incredible onslaught mounted by the Boros Legion as well as the Simic Combine. For the Boros player, curving out with efficient beaters like [Boros Elite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Elite), [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek) and [Wojek Halberdiers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wojek+Halberdiers) often pressured opponents to suffocation. The perfect draw of quality creatures which grew progressively ([Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudfin+Raptor), [Experiment One](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Experiment+One), [Shambleshark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shambleshark), [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura)) often caused opponents to fall behind, especially when supported by cheap pumps and support spells like [Spell Rupture](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Rupture).



![Zhur-Taa Swine++Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Zhur-Taa%20Swine&options=)
![Zhur-Taa Swine++Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Basilica%20Guards&options=)

The Gruul Clans made blocking decisions extremely difficult without [Smite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smite), courtesy of fatties who double up as bloodrushing pump spells. Despite being capable of being aggressive, the Orzhov Syndicate and House Dimir could also switch modes and play the defensive game, sometimes using Extort in conjuction with evasive creatures like [Basilica Screecher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Screecher) and [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) as a primary route to victory.



![Blood Baron of Vizkopa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Blood+Baron+of+Vizkopa)

With the introduction of *Dragon's Maze*, chaos seems to have been unleashed upon the entire drafting table. Players were greeted with a ton of options, and gold cards occupied higher percentage of the boosters. Juicy cards like [Blood Baron of Vizkopa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Baron+of+Vizkopa), [Advent of the Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Advent+of+the+Wurm), Gruul's War Chant, [Beetleform Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Beetleform+Mage), [Putrefy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Putrefy) and [Warleader's Helix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warleader%27s+Helix) quickly forced players to jump into two colours.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/turnburn.jpg)
The temptation to play both sides of split cards like [Far & Away](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Far+%2F%2F+Away), [Turn & Burn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Turn+%2F%2F+Burn) or [Ready & Willing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ready+%2F%2F+Willing) prompts greedy players to dip into their third or fourth (or even fifth) color, in order to transform their decks from decent into gamebreaking.



![Maze Glider++Smelt-Ward Gatekeepers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Maze%20Glider&options=)
![Maze Glider++Smelt-Ward Gatekeepers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Smelt-Ward%20Gatekeepers&options=)

Even the mono-colored cards encouraged players to play with more colors! The cycle of Maze elementals encouraged you to play with more multicolored creatures. The Gatekeepers forced you to grab Guildgates earlier than before, eventually tempting you to give in to your desires to optimize your picks by picking up cards of other colors. Removal spells like [Fatal Fumes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fatal+Fumes) and [Punish the Enemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punish+the+Enemy) were costed with only a single colored mana, possibly to encourage additional splashes.



![Gruul Cluestone++Golgari Guildgate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Gruul%20Cluestone&options=)
![Gruul Cluestone++Golgari Guildgate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Golgari%20Guildgate&options=)

Aside from the ubiquitous Guildgate (or the occasional [Shock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shock)land) in every pack, there is also an average of 1.66 Cluestones in each booster. It would seem that drafting a multi-colored deck with a bigger and more impactful cards was the direction that we're meant to be headed.


Several Pros have suggested to forgo synergy for "generally better" cards. The argument was that the "generally better" cards are "generally better" throughout the entire game, whereas small one drops and two drops quickly get outclassed. With the introduction of Gatekeepers, offensive creatures were invalidated more quickly than before and it was harder to get a deck full of the same keyword (for example drafting a deck with 10 Extort creatures or 10 Evolve creatures).


Today, players are greeted with an additional 156 cards to the mix and it marks the beginning of a new era. How will players adapt to a whole new world?




---

Saturday, 10.30 a.m. - Through the Ages: Bangkok Edition
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sin*

  
![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/fujita.jpg)  
*Tsuyoshi Fujita* 
Precisely ten years ago, trailblazer of the Japanese Pro Tour lifestyle, Tsuyoshi Fujita came and conquered the first ever Grand Prix to be held in Thailand. Piloting the resilient "Goblin Bidding" deck he had personally designed, he defeated (fondly remembered) Itaru Ishida in the finals to bring home the champion trophy. This event was especially significant for Fujita since it marked his TENTH Grand Prix Top 8, coupled with his first repeat Grand Prix victory.



![Patriarch's Bidding++Goblin Warchief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Patriarch's%20Bidding&options=)
![Patriarch's Bidding++Goblin Warchief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Goblin%20Warchief&options=)

Despite Japanese dominance at this 257-man tournament, the Thais managed to place two players in the Top 8, demonstrating that they were not pushovers and capable of putting up resistance!




|  |
| --- |
| Grand Prix Bangkok 2003 Top 8 |
| 1) Tsuyoshi Fujita |
| 2) Itaru Ishida |
| 3) Vincent Gan |
| 4) Osamu Fujita |
| 5) Masahiko Morita |
| 6) Tsutomu Yamada |
| 7) Peerapat Ekpoothorn |
| 8) Noppadol Srirattana |

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/morita.jpg)  
*Masahiko Morita* 
Correct me if I am wrong, but I believe Grand Prix Bangkok 2007 also marked the first and only time where the entire Top 8 consisted of solely Japanese and Singaporean players.


It also seemed that if you had lost in the Top 8 of a previous Grand Prix Bangkok, you have a decent chance of winning the next one. After failing to advance to the semifinals back in 2003, Masahiko Morita managed to win the whole thing this time. To this day, Morita holds the somewhat-bittersweet record for being both the player with the most number of Grand Prix Top 8s (sweet sixteen) and the most number of lifetime Pro Points without a Pro Tour Top 8.




|  |
| --- |
| Grand Prix Bangkok 2007 |
| 1) Masahiko Morita |
| 2) Shingou Kurihara |
| 3) Choo Yong Han |
| 4) Ong Kok Seng |
| 5) Junya Iyanaga |
| 6) Otsuka Kotaro |
| 7) Steven Tan |
| 8) Takuya Osawa |

Interestingly, Pro Tour Prague Champion, Takuya Osawa and Shingou Kurihara had earlier made Top 8 at Pro Tour Geneva together and the Osawa would also later go on to capture the next Grand Prix Bangkok trophy, which brings us to year 2009.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/kurihara.jpg)  
*Shingou Kurihara* 


|  |
| --- |
| Grand Prix Bangkok 2009 |
| 1) Shingou Kurihara |
| 2) Martin Juza |
| 3) Koutarou Ootsuka |
| 4) Matteo Orsini Jones |
| 5) Ruud Warmenhoven |
| 6) Yuuya Watanabe |
| 7) Ryan Luo |
| 8) Zhang Zhiyang |

To be crowned the champ, Kurihara had to defeat "very bad" player and full-time tourist Martin Juza, whom (at the time) had just lost in yet another finals against Oliver Ruel at Grand Prix Brighton a fortnight ago. This victory would be his first and only win among the five times he had made the final tables.


Judging from history alone, Grand Prix Bangkok has always been captured by the Japanese and other than the first one, it's victor was always someone who made the Top 8 previously. Going by this trend, our money is on reigning Player of the Year (and Platinum Pro Yuuya) Watanabe to win Grand Prix Bangkok this time! But honestly, it could be anyone's day and only time will tell!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/watanabe.jpg)  
*Yuuya Watanabe* 


---

  
  

 

Saturday, 12.15p.m. - Mystery Pro Toils in Trouble!
---------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

  
Someone has crossed the oceans and had misfortune of receiving the pool below. At first glance, there are an obvious lack of bombs and removal. Upon further inspection, it looks like it isn't easy to build either a beatdown or control deck. With scattered cards over multiple colors and way too many Cluestones, it looks like someone is in peril!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/mysterypro3.jpg)  
*Some cards you'd love to see in a Sealed pool.* 
How would you build this deck and do you think its any good? Maybe its not as bad as we think but it certainly isn't what we'd like to see at a Grand Prix! We'll reveal the identity of this Mystery Pro's and his final configuration at the end of the day, so stay tuned!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/mysterypro3a.jpg)  
*Some cards you'd rather not have!*

Round 3 Feature Match: Jake Hart vs. Weng Heng Soh
--------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

  
"There just aren't many better 2-drops than this little dude", said Jake Hart of his favourite insect, [Woodlot Crawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Woodlot+Crawler). Unfortunately for Hart, Weng Heng Soh was able to deal with the pesky forestwalker over the course of 3 games, taking the match 2-1.


That a diminutive 2/1 could be a focal card of a match featuring hordes of 6 and 7-drops indicates the power of protection, with Soh forced to find ways around and over the troublesome grub to win his games.


Soh began Game 1 with an [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian). Hart dropped a medley of Guildgates and a [Rakdos Signet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Signet), using a single black mana to efficiently [Killing Glare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Killing+Glare) the Guardian. Soh followed up with a [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath), while Hart summoned a [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) to keep pace.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r3_hart.jpg)  
*Jake Hart* 
Hart played out more mana rocks and summoned a [Woodlot Crawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Woodlot+Crawler), which impiously stared down its much larger cousin across the battlefield. Soh summoned an [Armored Wolf-Rider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armored+Wolf-Rider), while Hart had a [Tower Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tower+Drake). An [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict) took care of that.


Hart had a [Melek, Izzet Paragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melek%2C+Izzet+Paragon), which revealed a One Thousnd Lashes coming up for Soh's creatures. Hart went to trade his Longlegs for the [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath), but Soh saved it with a [Chorus of Might](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chorus+of+Might). An [Electrickery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Electrickery) took out Hart's [Rakdos Signet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Signet). Hart summoned a [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder), [Gruul Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Charm) took out the [Tower Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tower+Drake), and then Soh summoned an [Assault Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assault+Griffin).


"C'mon buddy, give me some good stuff on there", Hart begged the top of his library, which had so far spectacularly failed to do anything but let Soh know in advance what he was coming up against. Hart dropped the [One Thousand Lashes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=One+Thousand+Lashes) onto the Goliath, sending Soh's life total ticking down slowly.


Soh attacked and bloodrushed a [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager) to trample over Hart's blockers to beat the clock.


Weng Heng Soh 1 – Jake Hart 0


### GAME 2


Hart summoned his [Woodlot Crawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Woodlot+Crawler), which looked less useful against Soh's collection of guildgates. Hart cautiously sent in his abominable Insect and was relieved to have it connect. Soh dropped a Forest – prompting a brief cheer from Hart - before summoning his [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath).


"C'mon, little buddy! Don't die!"


Both players dropped mana rocks while the Goliath and Crawler stared each other down across the battlefield. Hart summoned a [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler)s and an [Opal Lake Gatekeepers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Opal+Lake+Gatekeepers). A Warleader's Helix took out the Revelers, while Hart had an [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest) for Soh's [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath).


A [Korozda Monitor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Monitor) from Soh was met with a [Maze Abomination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Abomination) from Hart. Soh maxed out his curve with a Spectral Primordial, grabbing the [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler) from Hart's graveyard. Hart promptly smote the Primordial with a [Killing Glare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Killing+Glare). Hart attacked, and Soh dual-blocked and killed the [Maze Abomination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Abomination) with his stolen [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler) and the [Korozda Monitor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Monitor). Soh tried to stem the bleeding with a [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm), but Hart had a [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging) for it, allowing his creatures to punch through for lethal damage.


Jake Hart 1 - Weng Heng Soh 1


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r3_soh.jpg)  
*Weng Heng Soh* 
### GAME 3


After an early [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging) to take out a [Greenside Watcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Greenside+Watcher), Hart hiccupped on land. Soh applied pressure with a [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager) and a [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm), while Hart cycled through detain effects with an [Inaction Injunction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inaction+Injunction) and a [Soulsworn Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soulsworn+Spirit). A [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder) kept the [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm) off the battlefield briefly, Soh carefully laying a spare Mountain before re-summoning the Wurm.


"You're going to blow me out with that [Electrickery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Electrickery)", Hart opined as he summoned his favorite [Woodlot Crawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Woodlot+Crawler).


Soh summoned his [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath), while Hart summoned a [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) and surveyed Soh's impressive board. [Punish the Enemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punish+the+Enemy) took care of the Crawler, and the [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) traded with Soh's Rampager. Hart was unable to answer the Wurm, though, and despite some last-ditch defense, fell a few attacks later.




---

  
  

 

Round 4 Feature Match – Chanpleng Sethsilp vs. Huang Hao-Shan
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

  
Affectionately known as "Vee" to his family and friends, Sethsilp Chanpleng is possibly this year's most "winningest" Thai player. After coming in 12th at Grand Prix Singapore, he followed up that performance with a Top 50 result at Pro Tour's Dragon Maze, good enough to edge out Nonthakorn Kositaporn to clinch the captaincy spot for the upcoming World **Magic** Cup.


Huang Hao-Shan on the other hand has had a mediocre season, seeing that he was unable to renew his Gold membership and would need to work doubly hard to stay on the train. However, Huang does have three Grand Prix Top 8s under his belt, proving that he was no fluke. At the very least, due to the improved Pro Player Club, being at Silver Level ensured that he would still be able to attend Pro Tour *Theros* in Dublin.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r4_sethslip.jpg)  
*Chanpleng Sethsilp* 
Both players exchanged their experiences at Pro Tour's *Dragon's Maze* and tried to determine who had the edge in this match.


"I went 8-1-1 at Block Constructed. Is that a good result?", Vee said cheekily.


"That's great, but this is a limited event. I went 6-0 in Booster Draft," was the quick retort, evoking laughter from all three of us before eventually settling on a unanimous agreement that it could be anyone's game.


### Game One


Despite being able to mount an extremely solid defense in the form of [Jelenn Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jelenn+Sphinx) and a [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer) (of [Serra Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Angel) proportions), Huang eventually succumbed to Vee's team of [Lotleth Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotleth+Troll), [Thrill-Kill Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrill-Kill+Assassin) and [Carnage Gladiator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carnage+Gladiator). Huang's white blue green deck which splashed red for [Blast of Genius](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blast+of+Genius) and [Punish the Enemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punish+the+Enemy) had only one solution to the annoying [Carnage Gladiator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carnage+Gladiator), which was the [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict) he failed to draw.



![carnage gladiator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=carnage+gladiator)

Sethsilp's first decision of the game was whether to use [Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devour+Flesh) on Huang's [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald). He contemplated whether he should allow Huang to waste his turn three creating a token, before pointing the "[Diabolic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diabolic+Edict)" at it. He eventually decided against that since he wanted to cast [Thrill-Kill Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrill-Kill+Assassin) and [Ogre Jailbreaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ogre+Jailbreaker) on his succeeding turns and maximize his mana utilization..


Huang had [Crowned Ceratok](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crowned+Ceratok) to force the trade and reinforced with [Jelenn Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jelenn+Sphinx) and a 4/4 [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer), but that did not stop Sethsilp's [Carnage Gladiator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carnage+Gladiator) and the unleashed Thrill-Kill from entering the red zone. Vee had [Trestle Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trestle+Troll) to hold back [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer) and all he had to do was attack every turn with his duo of regenerators, ensuring that Huang would lose two life even if both creatures were successfully blocked.


"Cards in hand?", asked Huang.


"One.", was the blank response.


Some people say the last card is always the best and it turned out that Vee's final trick up his sleeve was Soul's Ransom, splashed off [Izzet Guildgate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Guildgate). [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer) switched sides, but not for long since Huang decided that he wanted his flyer back. The ransom was Gruul Keystone and [Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) but this decision would later come back to haunt him for multiple reasons.


Firstly, there was [Blast of Genius](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blast+of+Genius) in Huang's hand he could no longer cast, now that he had discarded his only red mana source. Furthermore, it was revealed after the match that Huang actually had 12 other cards in his deck which cost 4 or more, which enabled him to use [Blast of Genius](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blast+of+Genius) to destroy [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer) while drawing himself two cards rather than giving his opponent two.


"I think I made a poor decision. I couldn't even attack with it. I could have waited until at least my draw step to see what I had drawn or activated the ability during his combat."


Vee 1 – Huang 0


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r4_shan.jpg)  
*Huang Hao-Shan* 
### Game Two


Despite having a deck loaded with powerful bombs and solid removal, Huang found himself on the receiving end of infamous mana screw. Despite playing a four color deck with multiple Guildgates, Huang had only two of his colors.


Having started out decently well with [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald) and a 2/2 [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer), Huang found himself stuck on 5 lands of the wrong colors (four Forests and a lone Island). Holding [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict), [Punish the Enemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punish+the+Enemy) and [Blast of Genius](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blast+of+Genius), he was visibly annoyed when his next draw phase served him a [Maze Glider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Glider) he still couldn't cast.


This gave Sethsilp enough time to power out [Haunter of Nightveil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Haunter+of+Nightveil) and [Maze Abomination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Abomination) using turn three [Gruul Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Keyrune). [Carnage Gladiator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carnage+Gladiator) once again reared his literally very ugly head and Huang had to peel something quickly. A Mountain or Plains would suffice but Huang had drawn a [Rakdos Guildgate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Guildgate), preventing him from advancing his board.


Sethsilp activated [Gruul Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Keyrune) and attacked with everything, representing at lethal damage. Both Huang and I knew he was dead since [Gruul Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Keyrune) was a multi-colored creature, which means it had both deathtouch and trample. All Vee had to do was assign one damage to Huang's blocker and the remaining two directly to him. Vee didn't see that play but it was inconsequential since Huang was already too far behind and even [Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Supreme+Verdict) wouldn't save him.


Vee 2 – Huang 0




---

  
  

 

Saturday, 6:40 p.m. – GP Bangkok Judging Staff
----------------------------------------------


*by Event Coverage Staff*

  
Behold! Our fantastic and incredibly good-looking judging staff for Grand Prix Bangkok 2013!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/judges.jpg)  
*Incredibly Good-looking Judges*

Round 5 Feature Match – Li Bo vs. Kuo
-------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

  
Both Team champions could not avoid the fate of being summoned to the Featured Match area before they could take their seats. In the end, it was Kuo Tzu Ching who defeated Li Bo in two games, largely with the assistance of [Maze Rusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Rusher).



![Maze Rusher++Morgue Burst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Maze%20Rusher&options=)
![Maze Rusher++Morgue Burst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Morgue%20Burst&options=)

### Game One


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r5_kuo.jpg)  
*Kuo Tzu Ching* 
Despite being ground down to just five cards in his library and a lowly three life, Kuo stole Game One on the brink of death, using the combination of [Maze Rusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Rusher) and [Morgue Burst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Morgue+Burst) to finish off an unsuspecting Li.


Both players had very controllish decks and nearly no damage was dealt during the few turns of the game. Both players had a suite of removal spells to answer whatever his opponent would present.


Kuo used [Ubul Sar Gatekeepers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ubul+Sar+Gatekeepers) to crush [Fathom Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fathom+Mage), giving Li a great target for [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound). Kuo reset the board with [Merciless Eviction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merciless+Eviction) to avoid bleeding to his death. Kuo sent Li's [Skarrg Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Goliath) on a [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) with [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict). The flurry of exchanges occurred to the point where both were simply waiting for creatures, waiting to be sent to the gallows.


"We're like two idiots doing nothing," Li literally laughed out loud.


Anyone watching the match could only nod and agree since neither could keep a creature on the board for more than a turn.


Li who seemed like he had the edge when he finally started to attack Kuo with [Crosstown Courier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crosstown+Courier), a card Kuo had deemed so unworthy that he had refused to kill. Despite being overloaded with great cards, he pretended like he was land-flooded, constantly commenting that he was about to die, continuing to take small hits from [Crosstown Courier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crosstown+Courier). I knew it was but a ruse since he was holding a fistful of removal, including double [Explosive Impact](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explosive+Impact), [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict), [Fatal Fumes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fatal+Fumes) and [Smite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smite).


While feigning weakness, Kuo was hatching a devious plan to finish of Li in one fell swoop.


When the time was ripe, he dropped [Maze Rusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Rusher) and slashed Li's life total by a third. When Li killed it with [Launch Party](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Launch+Party), Kuo resurrected it with [Morgue Burst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Morgue+Burst) to deal 6 damage to him and then attacking with the 6/3 once again, killing Li from out of nowhere! Li muttered some words under his breath, words we can't publish but everyone found supremely hilarious! Clearly, he did not expect to lose this way!


Li 0 – Kuo 1


### Game Two


Game two saw Li stumbling on mana and losing very quickly to a fused [Toil & Trouble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toil+%2F%2F+Trouble) for eleven "damage", coupled with a few attacks from [Thrill-Kill Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrill-Kill+Assassin) and one painful slash from [Maze Rusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Rusher).


Kuo led the game with [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) and Li replied with [Crosstown Courier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crosstown+Courier). Kuo voiced out his concern that his superior [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) was going to have to trade with "bad card" [Crosstown Courier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crosstown+Courier).


"If I attack, Li is probably going to block. And if I don't attack, Li will counterattack and I will be forced to block. Somehow the milling ability scares me even though its usually irrelevant."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r5_bo.jpg)  
*Li Bo* 
True to his prediction, both creatures traded in combat. This could only mean that Li had drawn his [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound). Now that [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) was gone, Kuo was left susceptible to it but it's not like he could play around it by not casting creatures, so he unleashed [Thrill-Kill Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrill-Kill+Assassin) anyway.


Usually, Li should be really happy since he had just found a perfect target for [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) but he didn't have a black source yet. He passed his next two turns in succession before being hit by [Maze Rusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+Rusher) once again. Using [Detention Sphere](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Detention+Sphere), he tried to relief himself the pain but [Toil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toil) & Trouble (for maximum DPS output) ensured Li would feel no more pain this match.



![toil // trouble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=toil+%2F%2F+trouble)

Li 0 – Kuo 2




---

  
  

 

Round 6 Feature Match - Matt Marr vs. Yuuya Watanabe
----------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

  
"Masterful" was Matt Marr's gracious description of Yuuya Watanabe's utterly annihilating play that took out their first game. Watanabe had come back from a precarious position to smash Marr for 18 points of unstoppable damage out of seemingly nowhere, and then went on to win the match 2-0.


Marr had sped out of the gates with a [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire), followed by a [Splatter Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splatter+Thug) and a [Boros Elite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Elite). Watanabe made a [Grisly Spectacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grisly+Spectacle) of the Thug, but Marr kept up pressure over the next several turns. Watanabe summoned a [Maw of the Obzedat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maw+of+the+Obzedat) and a [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways), but was unable to either attack effectively or stop Marr's Legionnaire.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r6_marr.jpg)  
*Matt Marr* 
Watanabe, heavy on lands but short on answers, could only pass and watch as Marr streaked further ahead. Sitting on a precarious 3 life and with only 1 card in hand, Watanabe would need to do something spectacular to get through Marr's army and barely-touched life total.


Then again, this is Watanabe. He drew his final card and paused for the briefest of moments before sacrificing his [Dreg Mangler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreg+Mangler) to the Maw of Obzedat. With the Mangler in the graveyard, Watanabe could scavenge it to further pump his Maw. With his remaining mana, he fuzed an [Armed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armed) and Dangerous, forcing Marr's impressive army to dedicate itself to blocking his Disciple. Once the Maw had sailed through unhindered, the Disciple got gobbled up by the Maw, which had grown large enough to finish Marr off with one ominous gulping sound.


Marr gracefully congratulated Watanabe before heading to his sideboard, shaking his head at the unexpected blowout.


Yuuya Watanabe 1 – Matt Marr 0


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r6_watanabe.jpg)  
*Yuuya Watanabe* 
Watanabe played a careful defensive game in the second, able to stop Marr from applying any real pressure, despite a [Gruul War Chant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+War+Chant) threatening shenanigans. A [Soul Ransom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Ransom) from Watanabe left Marr in an unenviable position, and his timely interception of a Hero's Mantle with a [Grisly Spectacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grisly+Spectacle) sealed the deal.


Yuuya Watanabe 2 – Matt Marr 0




---

  
  

 

Round 7 Featured Match - Sui Xin vs. Desmond Lau
------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

  
Sui Xin from China is no stranger to the Featured Match area. A well-respected cardslinger from Mainland China, he has been paired against relative unknown Desmond Lau from Singapore. Both players seemed to have the same level of understanding regarding the format though, since they had concocted up five-color control decks, laden with bombs, splashing for removal and card drawing spells.


Sui emerged victorious largely with the help of [Aurelia's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%27s+Fury) and [Teysa, Envoy of Ghosts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Teysa%2C+Envoy+of+Ghosts), surviving Lau's borderline-insane deck consisting of Hull of Vorel Clade, [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk), Soul Random, [Trostani's Summoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Summoner), [Alive & Well](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Alive+%2F%2F+Well) and double [Urban Evolution](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urban+Evolution).


### Game One


Lau had assembled a 16/16 [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager) using [Vorel of the Hull Clade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vorel+of+the+Hull+Clade) and [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage). However, Sui gummed up the board with [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) and waited until the very last opportune to tap down all of Lau's seven untapped creatures to swing for lethal.


Lau's draw was excellent and he managed to curve out perfectly, trailblazing with [Greenside Watcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Greenside+Watcher), [Tower Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tower+Drake), a Centaur token ([Alive & Well](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Alive+%2F%2F+Well)) as well as [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake).


However, Sui pacified the entire army by evolving [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) until it was capable of surviving even an assault against [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake). [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) was slowly sucking the life out of Sui but he was hatching another plan. All Sui wanted to do was put creatures on the board and lay in wait.



![Zameck Guildmage++Vorel of the Hull Clade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Zameck%20Guildmage&options=)
![Zameck Guildmage++Vorel of the Hull Clade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Vorel%20of%20the%20Hull%20Clade&options=)

Lau refilled with double [Urban Evolution](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urban+Evolution), eventually assembling a 16/16 trampler with flying. Sui pushed the 5/7 [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) to cushion the incoming blow, going down to three life and then during his upkeep, reduced to one precarious life due to [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound). It was then he decided to go for the kill, tapping down Lau's entire team for more than lethal.


"Well-played. Really," murmured Lau, seemingly convinced that he got severely outplayed by his opponent.


Sui 1 – Lau 0


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r7_xin.jpg)  
*Sui Xin* 
### Game Two


Lau opted to let his opponent play first and Sui punished that decision with [Stonefare Crocodile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stonefare+Crocodile), [Thrashing Mossdog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrashing+Mossdog) and [Alive & Well](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Alive+%2F%2F+Well). [Vorel of the Hull Clade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vorel+of+the+Hull+Clade) met with [Executioner's Swing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Executioner%27s+Swing) and Lau tried to race with [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) and [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager).


Sui once again unleashed [Aurelia's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%27s+Fury), killing the Rampager and reduced Lau down to exactly six life. If Lau chose to counterattack, the opposing Centaur token and [Thrashing Mossdog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thrashing+Mossdog) could be lethal if Sui had a trick.



![Aurelia's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Aurelia%27s+Fury)

Sui then dropped Teysa and wondered if Lau could deal with it this time. Lau topdecked [Soul Ransom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Ransom) while Sui had only a single [Putrefy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Putrefy) in his hand, which he used on [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk). He waited for a couple of turns before deciding to finally take back his Teysa.


When questioned why he didn't immediately take back the Teysa to try and win with the two-turn clock, Sui expertly explained that he had tried to delay Lau from drawing the two cards as much as possible.


"Sooner or later, I would need to give my opponents two cards. Why don't I give him those cards later? I was at 20 life and he was at 5. One false move and he could be dead."


Lau sought to seal the game with [Trostani's Summoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Summoner) but it arrived perhaps a couple of turns too late. Despite having [Turn & Burn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Turn+%2F%2F+Burn) to eradicate Teysa, time was called and Lau was unable to break past the defenses and extended the hand graciously.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r7_lau.jpg)  
*Desmond Lau* 
Sui 2 – Lau 0




---

  
  

 

Round 8 Feature Match: Kan Poonsattha vs. Liang Chen
----------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

  
Both games were how the Gruul-wielding Poonsattha wanted them: fast, bloody and brutal. Chen, hitherto undefeated, stumbled on defense against relentless pressure, and fell down in 2 games in very short order.


### Game 1


Poonsattha led play with a [Zhur-Taa Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Druid) and followed up with a [Boros Reckoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Reckoner), which Chen detained for a turn with [Azorius Arrester](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Arrester). The Reckoner waited a turn, then crashed into Chen unopposed. Poonsattha followed up with a [Cinder Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cinder+Elemental), while Chen had no further plays until his sixth turn, when he summoned [Mirko Vosk, Mind Drinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirko+Vosk%2C+Mind+Drinker).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r8_poonsattha.jpg)  
*Kan Poonsattha* 
Poonsattha had a [Traitorous Instinct](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Traitorous+Instinct) for the dangerous flier, and Chen decided to head for his sideboard rather than give up too much information in a game he wasn't looking like winning any time soon.


Kan Poonsattha 1 – Liang Chen 0


### Game 2


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/r8_chen.jpg)  
*Liang Chen* 
Poonsattha blazed out of the gates with a [Gore-House Chainwalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gore-House+Chainwalker) and a [Miming Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Miming+Slime), while Chen summoned a [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator). Poonsattha piled on the pressure with a [Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood)fury Giant and a [Pit Fight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pit+Fight) to take out the Manipulator, leaving Chen unable to recover, and the players shook hands and headed off for a break before the next round, the games having taken barely over 15 minutes.


Kan Poonsattha 2 – Liam Chen 0




---

Saturday, 9.30p.m. - Building a Sealed Deck with Mystery Pro (Lee Shi Tian)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*

  
We showed you [this](http://www.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gpban13/welcome#2) card pool earlier and it was owned by Lee Shi Tian, our Asia Pacific representative of the prestigious player Championships. As the Pro Point leader of the region, we thought it would be nice to take a look at his decision-making process.


He managed to make Day Two with the required magical seven wins, demonstrating that you don't need a ridiculously overpowered pool to advance as long as you build a deck with a focused concept.







#### Lee Shi Tian

##### Rare (1)



1
[Archon of the Triumvirate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BArchon%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BTriumvirate%5D)


40 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Island)



















![Wind Drake++Sunspire Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Wind%20Drake&options=)
![Wind Drake++Sunspire Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Sunspire%20Griffin&options=)

Despite allegations from himself that the deck is below average, he has managed to make Day Two with the following maindeck. His formula is not difficult to comprehend. A bunch of flyers like [Wind Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wind+Drake), tower Drake and [Sunspire Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sunspire+Griffin) race through the skies while annoying blockers like [Murmuring Phantasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murmuring+Phantasm) and [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) gum up the ground.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/shan_deck.jpg)  
*Lee Shi Tian* 
When the game spirals out of control, Lee will need [Gridlock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gridlock) or [Archon of the Triumvirate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archon+of+the+Triumvirate) to break the stalemate. A red splash allows him access to some light removal, as well as some combat tricks like [Scorchwalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorchwalker) and [Dynacharge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dynacharge) to occasionally steal games with his air force.


On hindsight, he could have chosen to splash black instead of red. "Playing black allows me to fuse Far & [Away](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Away), one of the best cards in the set. Along with [Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devour+Flesh), that is two additional "edicts". It also gives me two more fliers, [Rakdos Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Drake) and [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy), which is very important for my deck's concept." My opinion was that the black splash would actually be lighter on the mana requirement, seeing how you needed two red mana to cast Homing Lighting as well as activate [Scorchwalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorchwalker)'s bloodrush.



![Rakdos Drake++Far // Away](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Rakdos%20Drake&options=)
![Rakdos Drake++Far // Away](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Far%20//%20Away&options=)

Decent options if Lee chose to eschew red.


Regardless, he can now set aside his Sealed Pool as he advances to the draft tables tomorrow. Good luck Lee!




---

Saturday, 9.00p.m. - Quick Questions #2: Which is the best guild in Sealed Deck?

*by Chapman Sim & Pip Foweraker*

  

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_yasooka.jpg)***Shouta Yasooka**: Izzet is the best!* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_shan.jpg)***Huang Hao-Shan**: Golgari.* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_bo.jpg)***Li Bo**: Orzhov definitely.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_watanabe.jpg)***Yuuya Watanabe**: It's easiest to make a solid deck with Orzhov, but I don't know which is the best.* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_ching.jpg)***Kuo Tzu Ching**: Golgari.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpban13/qq_tian.jpg)***Lee Shi Tian**: Simic is best but that type of card pool is hard to open!*
